< Review>

Moving at the holidays is NEVER fun, much less so unplanned.  Dana Pruitt the PM and the rest of the team that I have interacted with so far have been nothing but attentive, responsive, helpful, cooperative and generally caring; not just for me, but I believe in their representation of their owner client.  I found the place on a Saturday, had a tour scheduled for monday, signed the lease tuesday and moved in on wednesday.  Dana helped this process move very quickly and efficiently with only the typical steps to take.  Since move in, they have been communicative and responsive about any repairs or issues to be resolved (given a bit of reasonable leeway over the holidays of course!) <rating>5</rating><Text>Taco Bell next door? Hard pass. Looking for a better taste? El Faro. Grab a large Jamaica or a delicious Horchata with your dependable quesadillas. Feeling adventurous with the new trends? Go there on the weekend only for some birria tacos that are possibly their most delicious items. Feeling like a philly cheese steak that's improved or a memory of a state fair cheese steak sandwich? Grab the steak and cheese torta and don't look back!

From nachos to dinner plates and even a shrimp burrito, you can't go too wrong here. I'm not necessarily a fan of the steamed tortilla but they're happy to grill upon request. Nor am I'm usually thrilled about their guac because it's a little thin for my taste. But I GUARANTEE once you taste their salsa you'll be hooked. You'll never look back next door for any fire or diablo sauce. Come grab an extra salsa that's laced with a hint of habanero and thank me later.

Enjoy a meal made with consistency and don't be afraid to say hi inside.< /Text>< Pics>

< Review>
Repair Bar is the best! My laptop's hard drive collapsed out of nowhere one day (it was a good eight years old), and I was terrified I was going to lose all of my work and personal documents, downloaded materials, and everything else I had saved. (My external backup drive wasn't working, either.) I brought the laptop in to Repair Bar, and the team there worked diligently for a whole week to retrieve my data. Since the repairs wouldn't be ready until after business hours on a Saturday, the owner offered to take time from his Sunday afternoon and meet me at the shop to give me the computer. About 95% of my data was recovered, and things are - thankfully - back to normal.

Great service, knowledgeable and communicative staff, and fair prices should make this your go-to place for repairs!<//Review>

<GmapID>0x80c2bb7f00df848f:0xf315355ad84c1d30< /GmapID><pictures>None<//pictures>< review>
This review is hot off the presses. Two weeks ago my iPad died. Battery drained. Wouldn't charge. I had about an hour's worth of video with my late, great aunt on that iPad that wasn't backed up. It would've been a terrible loss.

I took it to the Apple Store in Beverly Center. The Applebot did not try to plug it in or do any diagnostic. He simply told me that he could "feel a bump", meaning the battery had expanded and the iPad was dead. Data could not be retrieved. Sorry.

To Yelp! I found many listings for businesses that claim to do iPad repairs. Contacted four of them. 3 said, "Sorry, we don't do iPads." The 4th said, "Of course, bring it in."

I walked into the Repair Bar, a tiny storefront on Westwood Blvd just south of Wilshire and met the owner, Vess. I told him that all I really cared about was extracting the data. He was confident that was doable. I paid the $40 looksee fee (which is credited to any repair). A few days later, I was back to pick up my newly resurrected iPad. (The one that Apple Store had declared dead on arrival.) Vess told me it wasn't the battery or the charging port, but some little bit of circuitry on the motherboard. (If it's not one thing, it's a motherboard.) He also checked out the adapter and charging cable. Cable OK, but adapter had fluctuating voltage which is damaging to the electronics. He replaced the adapter for $25 (would be $60 or so from Apple).

The total repair came to $180. I would have paid $300 for the data extraction alone to get back those precious videos of Aunt Lou. But for less than $200 I have a refurbished iPad back with all the data intact, plus a new adapter.

Vess founded Repair Bar 10 years ago and has succeeded because he takes pride in the work and takes care of his customers. He provides an excellent service at a very fair price. Repair Bar fixes all things Apple: iPhones, iPads, MacBooks, etc. I'm confident saying that if your Apple product has given up the ghost and all appears lost, don't despair. Bring it to Vess at Repair Bar. I'm bringing him my "dead" MacBook Air next.< /review>

Note: This is a long story but 100% factual.
On 2/2/18 I called around looking to have my S7 Edge screen replaced. I finally stumbled upon Repair Bar, a SquareTrade certified repair shop, whom had the screen in stock. I dropped the phone off and paid 313.00 to have the screen/back glass replaced, and they asked me to come back a few hours later. After waiting several hours, they finally called and said it was ready. I went back to pick up my phone and ran into:

Problem #1 -- the soft keys did not work upon pickup. I demonstrated they did not work, and they took the phone back and said they would work on it. I decided to wait for them to fix it. After about an hour, they came back and everything was working. I left the store a happy customer.
After a month or so, I ran into:

Problem #2 -- the back glass slowly started to lift off of the phone. I attribute this to the hasty repair job, as he needed to remove the back glass in order to remedy the soft button issue. Instead of using a proper adhesive (back glasses come with a pre-installed adhesive that should be used once), the technician sloppily attempted to glue the newly installed screen on. I wasn't too worried at this point, because if I gave it gentle squeezes, it would re-stick and I would be fine for a few days before needing to do it again. I finally ran into:

Problem #3 -- a slight extension of problem #2. I was laying in bed looking at my phone and the back glass FELL OFF. So, I was stuck with a phone with no back. I was out of the country and unable to return to have them fix it. I purchased and replaced the back glass on my own. Around the end of April, I ran into:

Problem #4 -- The screen began to develop large purple lines across the length of the phone, approximately 1/3 of the way to the right. I called the Repair Bar back and they told me to bring the phone in. I brought the phone in, and they said no warranties, I must have caused the damage from "causing too much pressure on the screen." They would not stand by the repair.

TL;DR -- Paid top dollar for a screen to be replaced (well, Squaretrade did), was plagued with problems, and the company refused to stand by the repair. They are the only people in the LA area that stock the screen, but that is irrelevant if the repair is poor and fails within 3 months.<//Review>
